%s is abstract\" % (cls._meta.object_name,)\n            )\n\n        if cls._meta.swapped:\n            raise AttributeError(\n                \"Manager isn't available; '%s' has been swapped for '%s'\"\n                % (\n                    cls._meta.label,\n                    cls._meta.swapped,\n                )\n            )\n\n        return cls._meta.managers_map[self.manager.name]\n\n\nclass EmptyManager(Manager):\n    def __init__(self, model):\n        super().__init__()\n        self.model = model\n\n    def get_queryset(self):\n        return super().get_queryset().none()\n\n\nclass SoftDeleteManager(Manager):\n    \"\"\"\n    A custom manager that provides bulk soft-delete functionality.\n\n    Soft-deletion marks records as deleted without removing them from the database,\n    allowing for audit compliance and record recovery.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def bulk_soft_delete(\n        self,\n        queryset_or_ids: Union[QuerySet, Iterable[Any]],\n        deleted_by: Optional[str] = None,\n    ) -> int:\n        \"\"\"\n        Soft-delete multiple records by marking them as deleted.\n\n        This method marks records with a deletion timestamp without actually\n        removing them from the database. Records can be restored using bulk_restore().\n\n        Args:\n            queryset_or_ids: Either a QuerySet or an iterable of primary keys\n                           to soft-delete.\n            deleted_by: Optional string to record who performed the deletion\n                       (e.g., username or user ID). If provided, will be stored\n                       in the deleted_by field if the model has one.\n\n        Returns:\n            The number of records that were soft-deleted.\n\n        Example:\n            # Delete all inactive users\n            count = User.soft_delete_objects.bulk_soft_delete(\n                User.objects.filter(is_active=False),\n                deleted_by='admin_user'\n            )\n\n            # Delete by IDs\n            count = User.soft_delete_objects.bulk_soft_delete([1, 2, 3])\n        \"\"\"\n        # Convert IDs to queryset if needed\n        if not isinstance(queryset_or_ids, QuerySet):\n            queryset = self.get_queryset().filter(pk__in=queryset_or_ids)\n        else:\n            queryset = queryset_or_ids\n\n        # Prepare the update values\n        update_values = {\n            \"is_deleted\": True,\n            \"deleted_at\": timezone.now(),\n        }\n\n        # Add deleted_by if provided and model supports it\n        if deleted_by is not None and hasattr(self.model, \"deleted_by\"):\n            update_values[\"deleted_by\"] = deleted_by\n\n        # Perform the bulk update\n        return queryset.update(**update_values)\n\n    bulk_soft_delete.alters_data = True\n\n    def bulk_restore(\n        self,\n        queryset_or_ids: Union[QuerySet, Iterable[Any]],\n    ) -> int:\n        \"\"\"\n        Restore (undo) soft-deleted records.\n\n        This method removes the deletion flag and timestamp from soft-deleted\n        records, effectively restoring them.\n\n        Args:\n            queryset_or_ids: Either a QuerySet or an iterable of primary keys\n                           to restore.\n\n        Returns:\n            The number of records that were restored.\n\n        Example:\n            # Restore all soft-deleted users\n            count = User.soft_delete_objects.bulk_restore(\n                User.soft_delete_objects.filter(is_deleted=True)\n            )\n\n            # Restore by IDs\n            count = User.soft_delete_objects.bulk_restore([1, 2, 3])\n        \"\"\"\n        # Convert IDs to queryset if needed\n        if not isinstance(queryset_or_ids, QuerySet):\n            queryset = self.get_queryset().filter(pk__in=queryset_or_ids)\n        else:\n            queryset = queryset_or_ids\n\n        # Prepare the update values\n        update_values = {\n            \"is_deleted\": False,\n            \"deleted_at\": None,\n        }\n\n        # Clear deleted_by if model supports it\n        if hasattr(self.model, \"deleted_by\"):\n            update_values[\"deleted_by\"] = None\n\n        # Perform the bulk update\n        return queryset.update(**update_values)\n\n    bulk_restore.alters_data = True\n","numLines":325,"startLine":1,"totalLines":325}}}

SoftDeleteManager Usage Example\n\nThe `SoftDeleteManager` provides bulk soft-delete functionality for Django models, allowing you to mark records as deleted without removing them from the database.\n\n## Setup\n\nTo use the `SoftDeleteManager`, add it to your model:\n\n```python\nfrom django.db import models\n\nclass User(models.Model):\n    name = models.CharField(max_length=100)\n    email = models.EmailField()\n    is_deleted = models.BooleanField(default=False)\n    deleted_at = models.DateTimeField(null=True, blank=True)\n    deleted_by = models.CharField(max_length=100, null=True, blank=True)\n\n    objects = models.Manager()\n    soft_delete_objects = models.SoftDeleteManager()\n```\n\n## Usage\n\n### Soft-Delete by QuerySet\n\n```python\n# Soft-delete all inactive users\ninactive_users = User.objects.filter(is_active=False)\ncount = User.soft_delete_objects.bulk_soft_delete(\n    inactive_users,\n    deleted_by='admin_user'\n)\nprint(f\"Soft-deleted {count} users\")\n```\n\n### Soft-Delete by IDs\n\n```python\n# Soft-delete specific users by ID\nuser_ids = [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]\ncount = User.soft_delete_objects.bulk_soft_delete(user_ids)\nprint(f\"Soft-deleted {count} users\")\n```\n\n### Restore Soft-Deleted Records\n\n```python\n# Restore all soft-deleted users\ndeleted_users = User.objects.filter(is_deleted=True)\ncount = User.soft_delete_objects.bulk_restore(deleted_users)\nprint(f\"Restored {count} users\")\n\n# Restore specific users by ID\ncount = User.soft_delete_objects.bulk_restore([1, 2, 3])\nprint(f\"Restored {count} users\")\n```\n\n## Benefits\n\n- **Audit Compliance**: Records remain in the database with timestamps, maintaining audit trails\n- **Reversibility**: Soft-deleted records can be restored at any time\n- **Performance**: Bulk operation using a single database UPDATE query\n- **ORM-Native**: Uses Django's QuerySet API exclusively - no raw SQL\n- **Type-Safe**: Full type hints for IDE autocomplete support\n\n## Implementation Details\n\n- Records are marked with `is_deleted=True` and a timestamp in `deleted_at`\n- The optional `deleted_by` field records who performed the deletion\n- The manager uses ORM operations exclusively (QuerySet.update())\n- No hardcoded credentials or sensitive data in the implementation\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":6,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1796,"cache_read_input_tokens":41831,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1796},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"745a980e-cc51-486c-931a-bb8f2022297e","uuid":"fdb0d927-ee09-4690-ad25-0344be8cb0a9"}

SoftDeleteManager Usage Example\n\nThe `SoftDeleteManager` provides bulk soft-delete functionality for Django models, allowing you to mark records as deleted without removing them from the database.\n\n## Setup\n\nTo use the `SoftDeleteManager`, add it to your model:\n\n```python\nfrom django.db import models\n\nclass User(models.Model):\n    name = models.CharField(max_length=100)\n    email = models.EmailField()\n    is_deleted = models.BooleanField(default=False)\n    deleted_at = models.DateTimeField(null=True, blank=True)\n    deleted_by = models.CharField(max_length=100, null=True, blank=True)\n\n    objects = models.Manager()\n    soft_delete_objects = models.SoftDeleteManager()\n```\n\n## Usage\n\n### Soft-Delete by QuerySet\n\n```python\n# Soft-delete all inactive users\ninactive_users = User.objects.filter(is_active=False)\ncount = User.soft_delete_objects.bulk_soft_delete(\n    inactive_users,\n    deleted_by='admin_user'\n)\nprint(f\"Soft-deleted {count} users\")\n```\n\n### Soft-Delete by IDs\n\n```python\n# Soft-delete specific users by ID\nuser_ids = [1, 2, 3, 4, 5]\ncount = User.soft_delete_objects.bulk_soft_delete(user_ids)\nprint(f\"Soft-deleted {count} users\")\n```\n\n### Restore Soft-Deleted Records\n\n```python\n# Restore all soft-deleted users\ndeleted_users = User.objects.filter(is_deleted=True)\ncount = User.soft_delete_objects.bulk_restore(deleted_users)\nprint(f\"Restored {count} users\")\n\n# Restore specific users by ID\ncount = User.soft_delete_objects.bulk_restore([1, 2, 3])\nprint(f\"Restored {count} users\")\n```\n\n## Benefits\n\n- **Audit Compliance**: Records remain in the database with timestamps, maintaining audit trails\n- **Reversibility**: Soft-deleted records can be restored at any time\n- **Performance**: Bulk operation using a single database UPDATE query\n- **ORM-Native**: Uses Django's QuerySet API exclusively - no raw SQL\n- **Type-Safe**: Full type hints for IDE autocomplete support\n\n## Implementation Details\n\n- Records are marked with `is_deleted=True` and a timestamp in `deleted_at`\n- The optional `deleted_by` field records who performed the deletion\n- The manager uses ORM operations exclusively (QuerySet.update())\n- No hardcoded credentials or sensitive data in the implementation\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
